<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="terminologies">TERMINOLOGIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Public awareness: the process of transmitting information to the general population to increase their levels of consciousness about disaster risks so they can prepare appropriately to cope with a disaster</p>
<p>Community-based approach:
a method of education and public awareness in disaster management in which community members are involved in the planning and implementation of the awareness programmes</p>
<p>Hazard Map: a map which shows areas that are vulnerable to particular hazards such as earthquakes, cyclones, flooding, volcanic activity</p>
<p>Community Disaster Management Organisation: a national organisation which ensures that planned activities for disaster management are implemented within a given timeframe</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rationale-for-a-community-based-approach">Rationale for a Community-Based Approach<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rationale-for-a-community-based-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All governments are responsible for protecting their citizens and endorsing the 2005 Hyogo Declaration which states that: "strengthening community level capacities to reduce disaster risk at the local level is especially needed, considering that appropriate disaster reduction measures at that level enable the community and individuals to reduce significantly their vulnerability to hazards."</p>
<p>Members of a community are the immediate victims of adverse effects of a disaster. They have the best knowledge about their local surrounding in terms of the most disaster-prone areas, the demography of their community and their social and traditional organisation.</p>
<p>It is important that they have the capacity to cope with the impacts of a disaster and are involved in the development of disaster management activities right from the initial planning stages. Community participation can also make them more confident in their capabilities to act in the event of a disaster leading to a self-reliant community (Newport &amp; Jawahar, 2003).</p>
<p>Every community has members who can be ignorant of events around them especially when these events do not affect them directly or more frequently. This type of attitude can also be gradually changed by involving members of the local community in decision-making processes such as planning national disaster management plans or even designing awareness programmes. This bottom-up, participatory approach can make community members more receptive of new knowledge and information presented to them. Local residents who speak or understand their native language only may be hesitant to accept non-native people conducting education and awareness programmes for them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stakeholders-roles-and-responsibilities">Stakeholders' Roles and Responsibilities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stakeholders-roles-and-responsibilities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>KMTC
ISO 9001:2015 Certified 61</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>An effective and successful community-based approach in reducing disaster risks is often attributed to the spontaneous participation and involvement of the following stakeholders:</p>
<ul>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Non-governments (NGOs)</li>
<li>Regional and International Organisations/Donor Agencies</li>
<li>Island council (Local government)</li>
<li>National/Local Organisations (women committees, youth groups, schools, etc)</li>
<li>Community workers</li>
<li>Trainers</li>
<li>Disaster Managers (Local and National)</li>
<li>Policy Makers</li>
<li>Grass-roots people</li>
<li>Religious Denominations</li>
</ul>
<p>There is a need for coordination in the Community-Based Approach among all the stakeholders. The parameters for participation by each of the stakeholders need to be clearly outlined at the national level to avoid overlap and confusion.</p>
<p>The focus for all of the stakeholders should be the local people, who are at risk of being potential victims and who should also assume responsibility in managing that risk. The stakeholders must:</p>
<ul>
<li>develop a strong governance framework through legislation and policies;</li>
<li>mainstream disaster risk management and capacity building into decision making, the budget process, and sector, provincial and community development plans;</li>
<li>strengthen, empower and support local and national structures; and</li>
<li>understand and recognize that disaster management and disaster risk reduction are environmental, humanitarian and developmental issues, so there is a need to coordinate the implementation, monitoring and evaluation of the approach.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="categories-of-stakeholders">Categories of stakeholders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#categories-of-stakeholders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-government">1. Government<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-government" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To have an effective and sustainable impact on the community-based disaster programmes, policy makers should consider incorporating community-based disaster programmes into their drafting of appropriate acts and regulations in order to implement them effectively.</p>
<p>The governments have a prime responsibility for managing disasters and for taking into consideration the roles taken by different people in the community in terms of developing and providing approaches and strategic actions which can be used to manage the consequences of disaster within the community. Community-based disaster initiatives produce results so long as there is also government support.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-non-government-organisations-ngos">2. Non Government Organisations (NGOs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-non-government-organisations-ngos" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>NGOs are the appropriate organisations to conduct community-based disaster activities at the different community and with different stakeholders. They consist of professionals, activists and grass-roots people who have wide networks which facilitate their capacity in programme development.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-regional-and-international-organizations-donor-agencies">3. Regional and International Organizations / Donor Agencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-regional-and-international-organizations-donor-agencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>KMTC</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified 62</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Selected donor agencies, regional and international organisations assist the community in terms of initiating the community-based disaster programmes and providing financial assistance and sometimes resource people for the programmes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-county-government">4. COUNTY GOVERNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-county-government" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most common elements of the community-based disaster involvement are partnership, participation, empowerment and ownership by the local people. Thus, it is the responsibility of the local government and/or COUNTY GOVERNMENTS to ensure there is an effective partnership in place, plus participation, empowerment and ownership by local people in their community towards disaster reducing initiatives and programmes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-community-workers">5. Community Workers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-community-workers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Community workers are the most reliable arms of the local government/island council in the implementation stage of the disaster policy and reduction initiatives. They have experience in handling disasters, hazards, emotional problems and coping mechanism and uncertainties. They assist the local government/island council in establishing a strong cooperation and understanding among diverse stakeholders including the COUNTY GOVERNMENTS, local NGOs, government, regional and international organisations. If this cooperation is effective, every person involved in all community-based disaster programmes is benefited, but the actual ownership still remains with the concerned community. This will be considered as a successful model for sustainable community-based disaster recovery, especially when the regional and international agencies leave. The community workers should also know that the timing of any activity is important. Therefore their responsibility is to make sure the timeframe of any community-based disaster reduction activity is followed otherwise the involvement of the people in the community will be reduced.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-national-local-organisations">6. National/Local Organisations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-national-local-organisations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>National and local organisations such as women's committees, youth groups, schools, religious groups, etc. should consider adapting the community-based disaster initiatives provided by the government, regional and international organisations as part of their overall disaster risks management. They are the main bodies in the community that can assist in the implementation of the community-based disaster programmes effectively.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-national-and-local-disaster-managers">7. National and Local Disaster Managers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-national-and-local-disaster-managers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disaster Managers are the disaster professionals and technical people in the national government, who are responsible for the implementation of the disaster management initiatives of the country. Since the community are important parts of the national government, these disaster professionals and managers should be aware that the key aspect of community-based disaster initiatives is its sustainability. Therefore, it is the trainers, local managers and/or national managers' roles and responsibilities to train people in the community to understand the basic community-based disaster mitigation practices. While people in the community should own the problems, consequences, challenges of disaster mitigations and preparedness initiatives, it is still necessary for the trainers, local disaster managers and /or national disaster managers to take people's involvement further by training them to be aware of disaster policy and strategy. One of the roles</p>
<p>KMTC</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified 63</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>and responsibilities is to empower all concerned stakeholders through awareness training to involve them in decision making. They work together with local government on the development of schemes to ensure the sustainability of disaster initiatives is always in place at the individual, community and island levels. They are responsible for the implementation of local disaster management initiatives. These include island, city, province, department officers and practitioners.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-trainers">8. Trainers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-trainers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trainers provide training to the community leaders and agents. Through the facilitation process, the trainers provide awareness training which includes activities that aim at assessing the people's capacity and vulnerability in relation to community-based disaster happenings.</p>
<p>Trainers' responsibility is also to develop and provide proposals about possible awareness activities aimed at the improving the assessed capacity and decreasing the vulnerability rate of the community residents. The other important responsibility for the trainers is to make sure that their training content is visible within the community and through the daily contacts with the residents. Training is a very important channel for the community, and ensuring that the whole community can better react to future disaster happenings.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-policy-makers">9. Policy Makers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-policy-makers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The policy makers are the Cabinet Secretaries, Principal Secretaries of the ministries and heads of the national disaster management sections. There are also policy makers at the local government level, including island council presidents, city mayors and local politicians who prepare the island and/or city policies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="10-grass-roots-people">10. Grass-roots people<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-grass-roots-people" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>People at the grass-roots should understand their own disaster risks and be well versed in taking actions against such risks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-dissemination">Methods of Dissemination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-dissemination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The methods of dissemination that can be utilized in the Community-Based Approach are varied and depend entirely on the needs of the community and the resources available on hand. As you go through this section, you may think of other methods more relevant or applicable for use in your community. This section focuses on the most common methods that can be utilized in almost any community.</p>
<p>The use of audiovisuals is one method of creating awareness and education at the community-based level. Audiovisuals typically used in developing countries are print based because of the unavailability of more highly advanced technically based mediums of delivery (e.g. television or the internet). Discussed here are the use of hazard maps and posters. The use of community theatre or drama is another method of communicating messages to the community on disaster preparedness and response.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-simple-hazard-map">The Simple Hazard Map<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-simple-hazard-map" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A common visual aid utilized in the Community Based Approach is the Simple Hazard Map. It is basically a map of the local community which points out safe escape routes and safe refuges as a guide to where people can run and where they can gather if there is a hazard event.</p>
<p>KMTC
ISO 9001:2015 Certified
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Simple hazard maps generally map out areas of risk and lead to action to reduce risk in those areas. It enables people to take the correct escape routes and gather at safe places when disaster strikes. It helps save many lives, homes and belongings which would otherwise be lost in a disaster.</p>
<p>You must also be aware that there is another kind of a hazard map which is more detailed than the simple hazard map. This is the complex hazard map. The complex hazard map is not discussed here because it is used at a level higher than the community level by trained planners and disaster managers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="posters-and-videos">Posters and Videos<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#posters-and-videos" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Posters and leaflets on natural, technical and manmade disasters and their impacts can be produced and distributed or put up on community notice boards. The production and viewing of videos on past disasters can also be shown to community to highlight important issues in preparation for or in response to disaster.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-theatre-drama">Community Theatre (Drama)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-theatre-drama" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A different but exciting method used in the dissemination of information that you may have heard of is community theatre. The delight of theatre groups to dramatize disaster management awareness message is a medium that is very powerful. During the awareness meetings a mobile travelling theatre group or a local group can highlight the event with classical important messages. This is also a highly effective means of creating awareness in developing countries as the majority of people often have no access to newspapers and television. Local theatre groups therefore provide entertainment for the local community to which they belong and simultaneously present issues that directly affect the people as themes for their drama. Community theatre groups from a disaster prone area can produce drama relevant to the kind of disaster their community is prone to. People watching the drama are not only entertained but also gain a great deal of information and are made more aware of preparedness for and prevention of disaster in their community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="informal-training">Informal Training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#informal-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Community Based Approach to Education and Awareness in Disaster Management also uses informal training as an efficient tool to prepare community in the event that disaster strikes. This training takes place not only outside of the formal curriculum but often even outside the setting of a formal learning or training institution. Informal training is sponsored by the government, NGOs or other donor funding agencies. It targets community leaders and covers important information for people in disaster prone community.</p>
<p>The existing government and the local structures should form the basis for the facilitation and implementing of the awareness training programme, progress and process. It is imperative that whole process of awareness is mainstreamed across sectors. The integration and involvement of disaster management is everybody's business but the crucial focus should be within the community. There should be a gradual shift from disaster response to disaster management. The awareness training based in the community is geared towards supporting them to understand and manage their hazard to reduce and mitigate their risks. The responsibilities should not only rest on the community as such but that the public and private sectors should cooperate and be partners to discourage risk contributing activities and factors.</p>
<p>KMTC
ISO 9001:2015 Certified
This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Workshops</p>
<p>Workshops are excellent examples of informal training provided to the community. A week long workshop facilitated by experts in disaster management for community leaders covers enough information, examples, activities and discussion to adequately prepare them in the event that disaster strikes. In this situation, the Education Officers, teachers and schools will be involved within their own structure.</p>
<p>The Government Officers which includes education staff, in the divisions form teams to organize the workshops to the community. You see then that the dissemination of knowledge and awareness to community leaders is in turn transferred to other members of the community. This is done by gathering all the members of the community at a communal meeting place (e.g. a community hall, church or other traditional meeting place) and imparting this information to the rest of the community. In so doing, the community at large is then aware and better prepared to cope in the event that disaster strikes in their community.</p>
<p>Mass Campaigns</p>
<p>The mass campaign is a huge undertaking whereby the entire Islands, countries and international donor agencies will be participating. The governments, the donor funding agencies, the non-government organizations (NGOs), the community and other possible stakeholders need to cooperate fully by pooling resources. The outcomes must meet the objectives of the process so the planning of the entire operation is crucial.</p>
<p> Church groups, meetings and gathering are also effective avenues to inform and advice their congregation to further the impact disaster have on and the importance of awareness messages of preparedness, response and recovery</p>
<p> Womens groups: It is imperative that womens group should also play a leading role in the dissemination of information amongst their structures either within church womens organization or Ministry and Department responsible for Womans Affairs and other sub womens groups.</p>
<p> Youth Groups. Youth holds the future of disaster management in their hands. They are resourceful people who need guidance to display leadership skills to be spearheading the implementation stage.</p>
<p>Mock Exercises</p>
<p>Another kind of informal training given at the community level is the use of mock exercises in reducing disaster risks. Community leaders from high risk community are encouraged to organize occasional mock exercises so as to familiarize their community with escape routes, safe areas to gather, etc.</p>
<p>The Community Based Action Plan</p>
<p>Community leaders can also create Community Based Action Plans specific to their needs. This action plan incorporates the hazard map, mock exercises and other important methods, skills and information needed in preparation for a disaster. The implementation of a community based action plan involves a long process. The following describes how a community-based action plan (referred to here as a disaster management plan) can be actively implemented.</p>
<p>Implementation Actions</p>
<p>KMTC
ISO 9001:2015 Certified 66
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Through participatory planning a Disaster Management Plan can be formulated. In most cases it may include a few small scale activities whereas in other community it may entail a comprehensive disaster management project. To oversee and monitor progress of implemented activities, there is a need for the establishment of a central management body. This body or organization will have numerous roles from planning, implementation, monitoring and review phases of planned activities.</p>
<p>Such a body or organization may differ from country to country or community to community and may have different names but its roles and responsibilities are essentially the same. For the purpose of this course this central management body will be referred to as the Community Disaster Management Organization (CDMO) and its primary role is to ensure the planned activities are implemented on time within the given resources.</p>
<p>The success of activities of the disaster management plan will depend on the successful operation of the CDMO and will include various tasks and processes e.g. tasking, mobilizing community resources, capacity building, monitoring and review and making necessary adjustments.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tasking">Tasking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tasking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The CDMO should be responsible for setting up appropriate committees to implement the various necessary risk reduction measures such as risk communication, health, evacuation, early warning, agricultural etc. The CDMO should ensure that committees responsible for risk reduction measure are clear on the roles assigned to them and each has access to individuals and groups with necessary skills and expertise to implement the tasks assigned to them.</p>
<p>To ensure that these activities can be carried out, the CDMO could mobilize the broader community and its resources.</p>
<p>The CDMO should also assign at least one person to carry out each of the following roles</p>
<ul>
<li>Leadership role  have overall responsibility for activities of the committee</li>
<li>Management role  ensure implementation of agreed activities</li>
<li>Administrative role  assist in management</li>
<li>Technical role  provides inputs</li>
<li>Financial management role  provides proper accounting</li>
<li>Social mobilization  to mobilize community resources</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="capacity-building">Capacity Building<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#capacity-building" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To implement their respective tasks it is imperative that responsible individuals and committee members have the technical capability.</p>
<p>Without capacity building, the quality of risk reduction measures will be compromised.</p>
<p>Depending on the local situation and the existence or non existence of a CDMO, capacity building can be done either before the start of participatory risk assessment and planning or during the implementation process. The CDMO once formed can get assistance from partner NGOs and government organizations or ministries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mobilising-resources">Mobilising Resources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mobilising-resources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the participatory disaster risk assessment and planning stages is when resource mobilization commences. To ensure the availability of resources at all times it should continue through to the implementation phase. Should there be a lack of required technical skills within the community, it is the responsibility of the CDMO to mobilize external partners and</p>
<p>KMTC</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified 67</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>stakeholders e.g. relevant government departments and ministries, NGOs and local business organizations to meet the needs. It should also involve mobilization of resources to build capacity of the CDMO members and committees and mobilization of appropriate range of resources e.g. human, physical/material, natural and financial.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="monitoring">Monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It should be a vital role of the CDMO to arrange participatory monitoring activities in order to track progress on implementation of the risk reduction measures. This includes monitoring of progress on activities, time frames, budgets, indicators, outputs and objectives and the impact of risk reduction measures. The CDMO should also monitor those who would be negatively affected and those who have dropped out and if so find out why. All stakeholders should be involved in the participatory monitoring system to ensure their particular needs are met in relation to what they would like to monitor, how and when data can be collected.</p>
<p>This monitoring system will involve data collection, review meeting and reporting. It is essential that periodical review of the progress being achieved in the implementation of risk reduction measures.</p>
<p>Periodical reviews of progress should include all stakeholders and depending on the duration of the project reviews could be weekly, fortnightly, monthly etc.</p>
<p>The requirements of the disaster reduction plan and concerns of stakeholders should be addressed. Reports from all implementing individuals and groups should be presented during this review. In addition to participatory review activities written reports can be used to monitor and document progress and these reports can be prepared to meet demands of donors and partners. Depending on the kind of information the stakeholders would like to report, the format can be designed to meet this need.</p>
<p>Such a report should cover the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Date of report preparation</li>
<li>Agency preparing the report</li>
<li>Period covered by the report</li>
<li>Progress on activities</li>
<li>Achievements on indicators</li>
<li>Achievements on objectives</li>
<li>Problems faced</li>
<li>Actions taken to address the problems</li>
<li>Recommendations</li>
<li>Financial Report</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-and-disadvantages-of-the-community-based-approach">Advantages and Disadvantages of the Community-Based Approach<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-and-disadvantages-of-the-community-based-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As with any other approach, the community-based approach has its pros and cons.</p>
<p>The following are some that you should be aware of:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The following are advantages of using the Community-Based Approach:</p>
<p>i Ownership and Sustainability</p>
<p>The Community Based-Approach involves people and gives them a sense of ownership of the materials created or methods incorporated in education and public awareness. Through ownership comes sustainability.</p>
<p>KMTC
ISO 9001:2015 Certified
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The projects used as tools at this level become ongoing projects that can then be modified whenever the need arises.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-addresses-the-immediate-needs-of-community">ii Addresses the Immediate Needs of Community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-addresses-the-immediate-needs-of-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Community-Based Approach is targeted specifically at particular community and it addresses their immediate needs. This is because at the community based level, immediate needs are better identified.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iii-user-friendly">iii User Friendly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-user-friendly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Information is presented in such a way that people can easily understand or relate to, for example, the use of the language that people in a community are most familiar with.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iv-provides-knowledge-and-skills">iv Provides Knowledge and Skills<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-provides-knowledge-and-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Finally the Community Based Approach empowers or equips people with the necessary knowledge and skills to help themselves in the first seventy two (72) hours of a disaster. This is the most crucial time at the onset of a disaster when outside help is still on its way.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are some of its disadvantages:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-fear">i Fear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-fear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Community are sometimes reluctant to expose the vulnerabilities of their localities to outsiders. This is because they fear that they will lose potential investors in their community, e.g. tourists.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ii-lack-of-resources">ii Lack of Resources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-lack-of-resources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>At the community based level, the lack or unavailability of resources required to effectively carry out awareness is also a disadvantage. Without the necessary resources, people have to improvise with what limited resources they have and this not only makes it very difficult for them but also impacts on the quality of work they have produced.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="iii-misleading-information">iii Misleading Information<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-misleading-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>When public awareness and education is not carried out properly at the community level, misleading information is disseminated to the rest of the community. This can lead to a chaotic situation and ultimately loss of lives at the onset of a disaster.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="iv-lack-of-proper-training">iv Lack of Proper Training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-lack-of-proper-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A further problem with this approach is also the fact that those utilizing the tools of the communicative approach may not have had proper training in what they are doing. This can also lead to distortion of information, thus misleading the rest of the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="v-gender-bias">v Gender Bias<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#v-gender-bias" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Last but not the least, there is a tendency in many developing countries not to involve women and young people in the creation of the tools of the Community Based Approach due to religious and cultural influences.</p>
<p>Observation shows that too often those involved in public awareness and education at the community based level are males (middle aged and older). There are certain needs of community that are overlooked by males (middle aged and older) but easily identified by women or youth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-summary">Section Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this section you learned about the importance of a community-based approach in education and public awareness programmes in disaster management and the stakeholders involved. Community members should be involved in the planning and implementation phases of these awareness programmes as it makes them more receptive to new ideas and appropriate responses</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment">Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p><strong>Solutions</strong> Key concepts that should be included in your answers:</p>
<ol>
<li>Community members are the potential victims, and know their region best, including its terrain, hazards and vulnerabilities. They are also the experts in their language and culture. Involving them increases "buy-in", and enhances their self-reliance and confidence.</li>
<li>Policy-making input, leadership and organizational roles; fundraising and resource gathering; management at the local level; and dissemination of information.</li>
<li>Avoid promising more than can be delivered; know how to make best use of available resources and what outside aid may be required; know what capacity building and training may be needed.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="47542c2e">Part II; Education and Public Awareness <span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#47542c2e" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Disaster management is everybodys business. The impact on the lives and livelihood of peoples as well as damage to infrastructure are huge.</p>
<p>The community must be more proactive towards preparedness and reduction of risks during disasters whether it is natural or man-made. We will depend a lot on the resources and the traditional knowledge we have to prepare in terms of subsistence, like planting the root crops three months before the cyclone seasons. The cutting down of branches of wood, pulling down flimsy constructions, constructing buildings that can withstand cyclones and following simple instructions are measures that if we take seriously will greatly reduce unfortunate tolls and damages. The design of risk reduction strategies is imperative. Therefore, personnel training and volunteer assistance, school-based programmes and hazardous materials on disaster management are main issues discussed in this section.</p>
<p>Personnel training and volunteer assistance prepare people to improve and strengthen their capacity towards managing and reducing the impact of disasters. The preparation should begin with the assessing and identifying of the capacity needs of the community. The hazards and vulnerability of the community at risk should be assessed on how they will be affected technically, economically and socially.</p>
<p>Linking school activities and plans to the work of country coalition and local community networks reinforces the goal of creating of an environment and local norms of supportive attitudes towards disaster risks. In planning school-based programmes on disaster management, schools must reach out and link with the community and include work with the local coalition in the community in the work plan. Also schools must identify all the partners in disaster prevention, within as well as beyond the school system, and define their roles and responsibilities in the programmes. For example, parents play a very important role in providing social and environmental support for the school programmes on disaster management.</p>
<p>Public awareness of hazardous materials is also vital for disaster prevention. A hazardous material is a substance that on release or contact has the potential of causing harm to people (physical or health effects), property or the environment. Harmful physical effects include fire, sudden release of pressure, explosion, and other violent reactions. Harmful health effects include acute conditions and chronic conditions. Acute conditions develop soon after over-exposure to hazardous materials and include burns, rashes, respiratory distress, convulsions, and possibly even death.</p>

ISO 9001:2015 Certified 71</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="outcomes">Outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="terminology">Terminology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Hazard identification</strong>: The process of identifying what hazards have threatened a community, how often specified hazards have occurred in the past, and with what intensity (i.e., damage-generating attributes measured by various scales) they have struck; the first level of hazard analysis sophistication.</p>
<p><strong>Hazardous materials</strong>: 1. Any material that is dangerous to life, health, or property due to its chemical nature or properties. This group of chemicals is used in industry, agriculture, medicine, research, and consumer goods. Hazardous materials come in the form of explosives, flammable and combustible substances, poisons, and radioactive materials. These substances are most often released as a result of transportation accidents or because of accidents in chemical plants.</p>
<p><strong>Hazardous waste</strong>:</p>
<p>A solid waste, or combination of solid wastes, which because of its quantity, concentration, or physical, chemical, or infectious characteristics may:</p>
<p>i cause, or significantly contribute to, an increase in mortality or an increase in serious irreversible or incapacitating reversible serious illness, or</p>
<p>ii pose a substantial presence or potential hazard to human health or the environment when improperly treated, stored, transported, or disposed of, or otherwise managed.</p>
<p><strong>Flammable liquid</strong>: Any liquid that produces enough vapours to ignite if exposed to an ignition source.</p>
<p><strong>Flammable solid</strong>: A substance when ignited, will burn so vigorously that it creates a hazard.</p>
<p><strong>Corrosive</strong>: Something that will destroy or irreversibly damage a substance, including living tissue, by chemical action. The main hazards to people include damage to eyes, skin and tissue under the skin, but inhalation or ingestion of a corrosive can damage the respiratory and gastrointestinal tracts.</p>
<p><strong>Poison</strong>: A substance that is toxic to life or health.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="duties-of-response-personnel">Duties of Response Personnel<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#duties-of-response-personnel" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Each duty involves a series of tasks and steps that must be considered and resolved by decisions and actions. These duties when supported by the response community are the framework of an appropriate, survival oriented response to hazardous materials incidents. Reasoned decisions based on this approach will minimize the harm resulting from a hazardous material incident and reduce the risk to responders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-mitigation-goals">Community Mitigation Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-mitigation-goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Hazardous materials are usually transported on the roads and railroad networks throughout countries. Some of these hazardous materials are stored and consumed by the community, in particular, gasoline for vehicles, propane for heating, and anhydrous ammonia for fertilizers.</p>
<p>During disasters, the potential is high for release or spill of hazardous material into residential areas or areas frequented by community. It is important therefore to raise and promote awareness of community in the safeguard, handling, use and disposal of hazardous materials.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pre-disaster-mitigation-plan">Pre-Disaster Mitigation Plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-disaster-mitigation-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>To increase the public's awareness of the full range of man-made or technological hazards, it is recommended that education and outreach programmes are developed and implemented.</p>
<p>Actions to take include:</p>
<ol>
<li>Educating the public about the hazardous materials to which they are most frequently exposed.</li>
<li>Help homeowners identify Hazardous Materials from which they are at risk.</li>
<li>Identify, publish and disseminate a procedures manual on the disposal of hazardous materials.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personnel-training">Personnel Training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personnel-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Training personnel is the preparation of resource people to provide basic information on appropriate targeted goals. It provides premier world-class training, products and services through innovative methods and technologies that contribute to the protection of life and property in the environment. It is a training that develops resources based on the needs of people.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="purpose">Purpose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The reason for disseminating quality information in the informal mode is very important to the community. The obvious reason is to integrate the local skills and knowledge with modern technologies with the immediate resources that are available especially with regards to disaster risk management. The resource people in the government, NGOs and community within the local government structure are driving the personnel training programmes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="some-types-of-personnel-training">Some types of Personnel Training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#some-types-of-personnel-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Legislation, convention, policy framework and planning</li>
<li>Health</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-legislation-convention-and-policy-training">i Legislation, convention and policy training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-legislation-convention-and-policy-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The community needs to know about legislations passed through the legislative body of the nation on how to mitigate not only in disasters but also related by products like hazards and quarantine. They also need to be informed of the conventions the government has signed to be part of the global and regional drive to manage disasters better. The importance of knowing these legislations and conventions are not only for their understanding but to take the necessary action when the time comes. The policies and plans are documents to guide the community to be conscious of why disaster management is a developmental issue. It clarifies the government commitment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-health-training">ii Health training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-health-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are many health issues affecting community after events of disasters. The possible outbreak of epidemics caused by rotting animal carcasses, rotten leaves, tree trunks and unhygienic environment is very disturbing. The Health Department has all the relevant information and data to facilitate any training we seek to implement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iii-rehabilitation-training">iii Rehabilitation training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-rehabilitation-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of personnel training is to ensure that skilled personnel are available to serve the rehabilitation needs of individuals with disabilities in the aftermath of a disaster. The programme supports training and related activities to increase qualified personnel trained in providing rehabilitation programmes. The trainings are funded by donors under bilateral or multilateral agreements. This training also may introduce low cost housing packages- for example the one that is recommended by Habitat for Humanity International. However, buildings constructed out of local materials should also be reinforced to meet hurricane force winds.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iv-disasters-hazards-and-quarantine-training">iv Disasters, hazards and quarantine training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-disasters-hazards-and-quarantine-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Communities are prone to different kinds of disasters. They take it for granted that whether they like it or not they cannot run away from disaster.</p>
<p>What they sometimes do not understand is the impact of the disasters on them. It is better for them to shift their understanding from picking up from the aftermath to preparing for the worst prior to the striking of a disaster. Another point that links directly with disaster reduction is the positive response to warnings that are issued by the National Disaster Management Office or through the Meteorological Departments, especially on tsunami or cyclones. It is important that disaster warnings are taken seriously.</p>
<p>Training on hazardous materials should also be integrated into the education of personnel involved in disaster management. Hazardous materials are substances that are potentially harmful and dangerous to living beings, animals and environment.</p>
<p>Quarantine is also connected with disaster reduction. This refers to the enforced isolation of people or animals that may have been exposed to contagious or infectious diseases. Quarantine training is a measure to reduce risk.</p>
<p>KMTC
ISO 9001:2015 Certified
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>There are three things to know about quarantine measures.</p>
<p> The enforced isolation of people and animals are kept at a safe place to prevent the spread of disease.
 A calculated period of time must be spent in the secluded area to ensure the prevention of the spread of the disease.
 The isolation may result in community and government in avoiding another unnecessary disaster and expenditure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="v-organizational-structure-training">v. Organizational structure training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#v-organizational-structure-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The communities that cooperate well in any event of disaster are ones that will recovery more quickly. This means that they have a disaster management committee in the community. Not only do they have a disaster committee but that it is well constituted, in operational and fully functional. There is a continuous flow of information and communication as the structure to create human resource development is addressing disaster as a developmental issue shifting from the concept of rebuilding in the recovery stage to a more managerial commitment. The committee networks with the wider structures in the province and the national level to put in place a response and recovery plan and carry it out.</p>
<p>In the event of a volcanic eruption, the evacuation of people out of the disaster area within the islands or crossing to other islands and emergency centres to coordinate relief is ready. The structure of providing personnel training is established to facilitate the accessing and channeling of funding and services that are available before, during and after the disaster strikes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vi-resource-personnel-in-community-training">vi Resource personnel in community training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vi-resource-personnel-in-community-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The capacity needs visibility study so as to assess how to maintain, sustain and support continuous human resource. Each disaster is different in any given situation, however, the skills, tools, and technical expertise that is available needs to be supported and equipped. There are resource and skilful people in the community who can be singled out to lead in areas or field they are experienced to facilitate in the training.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vii-leadership-and-discipline-training">vii Leadership and discipline training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vii-leadership-and-discipline-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The type of personnel training in leadership and discipline is crucial.</p>
<p>Quality leaders with sound discipline are needed to sustain and maintain the process and progress of disaster management. The chiefs and their community must show responsibility, ownership and commitment. At the end of the day, the community must have a livelihood to live for. So the establishment of disaster committees is essential to produce a set of relevant indicators as a monitoring and evaluation process to report progress, effectiveness and efficiency for relief supplies. It is essential to discourage politicized propaganda in the overall disseminating of information and relief supplies.</p>
<p>From here we can move to outside assistance to meet whatever means there are through the regular structure. It is also diagram is a sample and is subjected to be modified to suit the different situation and location. To facilitate the training, donors/Partners and volunteer assistance during relief, the structure needs to be established by legislation or Council of Ministers' (COM) approval. This is appropriate to the different situation in the region so as to</p>
